des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Here is the translation of the text:
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	"And when there is one or more, they are far from the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are far have little moisture,"
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	"And then cut them with a little yellow water or a little blood, and their color is that of the flesh;"
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	"And the cure for those who have them deep in the foundation is that you command the patient to sweat by applying heat to the feet until the foundation is removed and the fluid comes out;"
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and hold it like a claw, or if you hold it with your fingernail, then cut off its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ligature cannot hold them due to moisture, take it from a scarf, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and hold them with your two hands, then cut them off, and powder them with any hot powders that are in the fire's place;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you may cauterize them as it is said or with a cautery paste, then cure them with other cures until they are well;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot be extracted, then cauterize the patient with a hot cautery and sharp so that it washes out what is in the foundation, so that it can be extracted freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Now if the disease is pressing on the patient, and its roots are deeply rooted in the foundation, then the treatment is easy;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you should press them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them off, then treat them as we have said, until they are cured, and do not incise them with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you bring the stitch according to this method: take a twisted thread and put it in a needle, then tie the thread at the top of the needle, and pierce the needle from another side, and turn the two ends of the thread over the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is a large one; then pull the thread up, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one.i. to draw out the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation.i. dampen it in oil or wax, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient that he rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it is healing, and when it has healed, if he cures with ointment and other cures, until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	on the foundation itself;
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Several times there is drying up of the ends in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you should scrape the bark off a tree or your nail, which does not allow it to moisten;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as long as it is sore, so that it may be well;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be healed, then shave it more vigorously than before, until it bleeds and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then treat him until he is well.
dou fremit	he fidgets
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	is a small appearance before the neck, and goes very well with it.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and it never breaks the skin, and you can feel it as if you were dead, and goes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is such that you take a feather from an goose, or a feather from a strong vulture, and put that feather on the wound, until the purple circle completely covers the wound.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand to all the feather as you cover the whole wound, and put it on completely, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cut of a feather of air or iron according to this form, and be subtle and draw it across:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, so that you may hold the two together, and press: And if you see, cauterize the wound, as it is before or of the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No clister made of silver or bronze, or of melted gold or brass; and no instrument of any size is appropriate, but only those for which it has been prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These, then, are the ones that are brought for the care of infants and weak or painful things, and are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the clister should be small and large if it is over the breast, or tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and I have a distention where the belly is tied up, so that you see it, and the ribs are pierced on one side, and in the other 1.8;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be massaged with oil of beans or parchment, and be pierced all around the small perforations;
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and let there be 1.8 inches of space between each perforation, then insert a strong wire mesh into these perforations and join the belly together as if it were a deer;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument lies before a strong wire, then cauterize it; and it takes the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil of olive or of almond nut or some other thing, then pour it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then have the ministers spread it on his head with their two hands together until it is completely coated, then remove the cloth, and hold the patient's legs against the wall,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine remain on him as long as he can tolerate it; and if he sleeps all night, that is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cauterize him for a disease of the belly that comes on gradually, and let the medicine remain on him until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if hemorrhoids are at the foundation or abscess, so is the clistere also very small like a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the clistere which is very small where the skin is tightened:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the cure of wounds; now we will tell you about the cures of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and because of this they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things for which wounds are made are by a blow of stone, and by a sword and knife, or a cock's beak, or a lance or spear or axe or scythe or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made by the blows of a horse's hoof, or of a whip, or of a staff, or of a hammer, or of a mallet, or of a similar object; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar parts;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, since the reminder will come in my chapter on this topic.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound occurs where the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or similar thing, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt about the incision of an abscess: if it does not cause great pain to the head immediately after the blood has come from the wound, and it hurts in the opposite direction from the part that was injured;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patient's appetite for wine and fatty foods is lost.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not salivate, if his meat is not increased, and he does not drink wine or eat cheese.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and over the wound, if there is an abscess, cotton wet with oil soak up, or wine stiptic;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, if it is fresh all over the body, and does not move with air, powder, which I will say a little hereafter;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it has been moved, if it is placed on some onions, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword's edge and similar, and the lips cannot be joined by sutures, if they are joined by stitching, as I will say about wounds from the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone and dries up quickly, then cure the wound with medicine and restore it with hard leather instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large, cooked meats such as testicles and wheat, as well as poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rot on the leather, and it doesn't touch the bone, then cut it all off, and throw it away, and then cure it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if he has an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting it, and he cannot stop the bleeding with medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it up like a knot.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if he does not benefit from it, then cautery him.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is: and that you put this powder which hardens so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood 2 parts; live coal 3 parts, and the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and hold it firmly, until it is well healed and joins together all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then put it well, and leave it not tied up if it does not swell, for we do not remove the medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make a cast of salt when you have the resin or dragon's blood, but let the arm not move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arm has moved the wound, nevertheless it is necessary to put on this powder, otherwise
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestives oils or flour of barley made with water and honey, as long as it is still wet;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the doctor prescribes other remedies until he is well.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the throat
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes from the throat and is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the wound is in the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the neck, if there is no other impediment to the cure, and do not put anything restricting, for this hinders the healing of the neck and makes it retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the neck is cold, and its extension with the brain, which is the highest limb;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but if the medicine is hot, like warm water mixed with rosewater and oil, and also cooked water;
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of my own according to this way, and wetting oils.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if the cut requires binding, then heal it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the animal is full of bowels and blood;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, if the fever and the loins and the cauterization are done;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the throat is blocked, so that the food does not go down, and the windpipe is closed,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if the food gets stuck in the throat, and does not touch the throat but puts it back according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then let it rest for a few days, and then treat it with garlic until it is well;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then examine it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can't bear it all, and what you cannot bear, leave it until the wound pus
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and be careful and rigid about the discharge;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle the powder that I mentioned on it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as described in my chapter onchapstick.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or a sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's from a spear or a sword, and the wound is deep, then check the patient's breath to see if they are still alive: know that such a wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if the wound isn't deep and is still fresh, then in the first hour don' t apply powder, nor tie it up so that the patient doesn' t die perfectly:
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and turn to face the patient, and take a breath yourself.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I feel a tingling sensation, and it lies there .ij. times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not feel any pain, put in the wound cotton wet with vinegar to absorb the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient lie on the wound .ij. times, or .iiij., or more often;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor a strange trembling of the heart due to pain;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good arrangements, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds of tents and other things, as long as he is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and if it bursts, know that there is a fistula; and if the cure is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a knife or a sword, and it is simple, or deep or on the back, if the cure of this one;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not infected, then let the wound rot, and then bring the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	and the rupture of the womb
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great and small and little.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a great wound there often springs none of the intestines, or from the innards, through which enters the efflux of blood;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitch is more painful, and never lessens the small wound than the great one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	For thus do we not put the intestines back in place, if we do not put them back in turn from warm to warm;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	for so that the intestines swell until they feel cold, if return more to the needles,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and so it hurts that the pain is great, and remain so in the needles, for I keep the intestine in its place than others .ij.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to .iiij. ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the .ij. common sutures have in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and he sews up the other wounds of the chest and .ij. other common sutures are equal to those of others;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and each is more proper with the sewing of the belly, and I will say each and I will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestine outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and good thing is to treat it, this is by one of the .ij. ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	Here is the translation of the provided text:
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in a certain way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Soak a sponge or cloth in lukewarm water, then wring it out slightly,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	Here is the translation of the text:
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine as much as it swells until it is osted;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and no time does this vin restraining, and is muder than a soul for disinfling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or salt and cook them well,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this the entrance to a little thing is blocked;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then cut a little hole in the wound with the instrument with which one cuts the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is to moisten it so that it heals;
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	so we do not have to cut it unless there is great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for breaking:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut it in the hollow and not on the outside, and see the shape:

Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you join the .ij. stitches of leather and the .ij. stitches of medicine together with a needle with a strong, flexible thread;

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or which he is

mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirror due to madness opens so much that it covers the abscesses.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrode a lot of matter and become a fistula, and I came so much that all fell off bowels and moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many I cured within two years, and there was no cure in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	for as long as I was called, and I saw a leg and the medicines that were used to treat it,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and he who runs through the pores with great speed.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red on the youth's body, and had an orange-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent in one of these pores, and then searched all the pores
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that one came together with the other on both sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and I dug into one of the pits as much as I could to uncover a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it rotten and broken, and the decay went up to the bone itself;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew that the bone I was holding was rotten, and I made sure that there was no other decay in it, except for that which I had already found;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and I could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continuing corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I held it, and leaned to mend the break;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not hold it with my hand on one side of the bone, and so I took it all the way down;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	and then I put medicine on it; and he was healed and completely mended,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and do not wish to repeat the work further than for the weakness of the disease, which cannot bear,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For in the work there is often blood evacuation, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and gave birth to bone in place of the bone, and was of good disposition and did not cause harm or adversity from all things, nor did it have any bad effects.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if his jaw is broken anywhere near the neck, then it should be done in this way:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take .i. a string, and tighten it at the top of the bone that has opened,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and order anyone that he extends it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another string of a larger size on top of the first string and tie it to the joint that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and set the head, so that you take the broken cart to the repairer,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the cart on the ground where you see the rope, so that the rope does not damage the cart;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place .i. log or a tree root underneath to support the cart so that it does not tilt;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and come as often as you can see and feel the corrosion, and come another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if his nose is corrupted, and does not open any more, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then discover the cart all; then put .I. a hot iron,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then silk from one part to the other the corruption, and be the silk sure from the long of the corruption .I. hole, if as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, so cut the joint corrupted, and silk the bone or it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption is in the continuation of the 19 joints, then there is another injury than an ache from copper.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if corruption is where it is poked with the hand, or where it is poked with the foot, then that is very painful.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but above all you must inquire about that corruption, how it hurts you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not hurt you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and you know that the chisel and the fibers to cover those bones are many, according to the appearance of the bones and the shape of the teeth.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for each type of work, there is a suitable tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and you know that the work will teach you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you use the instrument for which you are skilled according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	light a fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head should be positioned either towards or away from the fire;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicine, this corruption by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that member until the place where the corruption comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes from death or evil, which is greater, from the fault of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, and seems to be burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, then goes those correlations of the member from one to another.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and take it all over the body; if you hurry to cover,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if by the percussion of certain poisonous animals, such as
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the head of the two, if it jumps, and does not give it space to come by hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the cupping glass touches the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes up to the arm, so that the cupping glass touches the neck; and if it passes over the neck, then it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and do not wait for the quantity of its virtue
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and if it comes up to the first joint, so that the cupping glass touches the second joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to earth, so cover all the earth.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, so cover at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, so there is no other injury but to make the patient die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cover or sew the member so that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister one of the lines down, and another minister the other line up,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you remove the chaps between the 17th and 20th lines to a large 1st stake, as long as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the cap or silk, and place a lin cloth on each side, so that the silk does not touch the shoulder;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring the other injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood loss occurs when you work, let the area be cauterized thoroughly.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Or if there are any powders that restrain it, then return to your medicine until it is finished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bandage the member with a convenient ligature and treat it until it is well.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you that he came to Earth in the body of a man:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a blackness which seemed like fire burned him.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his two feet, as much as it stained all of the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the honourable man saw the corrosion, he took off the copper from the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that the corruption returned to his two hands, and came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and to me he sits on things that reflect after purification of the body, and cannot stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he ordered me to cut his hand, and I do not know how to hope that matter will reflect again;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he might die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the power of man is feeble; and he was despairing, and returned to his land;
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and wrap his hand with copper, and he was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I do not know but that for this reason only that someone else does something, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No time comes when the flesh is cut open, and remains so long that it makes a great assembly of bowels;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then rot and pierce, and in the process the bowels jump out, and remain so long that our vassals;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the leather which is above it is also very soft like.i. drapelets deliquescent,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not corrode as far as the bone, nor as far as the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and cook it so you chop all of the leather, and most importantly when it is thin, as well as our blankets;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not start for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have promised that the leather will be dried, and the corrosion is not yet complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the leather is tough like horsehide, so cook it with this mixture:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if her breasts are large, and the breast that gives milk has a putrid odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Therefore, the medicine made in Egypt, which is thus prepared:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take likewise, and oil, and lead-ore, equally, and put to cook in .i. vessel on the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and the make it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in cauterizing the chest, and extract the perforation;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for .ij. hours, then remove it by squeezing it out;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this mutch times, until the breasts are white, and the milk is stopped;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never is it clisted with water from ash,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you squeeze ashes from vine wood and pour water over them,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then pour it out, and clisten it, until you know the sinews are well-clisted;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes will help him.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the cauterization is with water and honey where there is a little bit of lead powder crushed.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you the cauterization with honey and wine honeyed, that honey has property of purifying and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine brings the blood to its place.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have promised that the breast is well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the cauterization of a woman who has given birth to a horse in her womb
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you squeeze it with oil and rose water and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cauterize it with certain medicines and herbs, of which I have spoken in the chapter on the treatment of herbs.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if it is small, and the cauterization wound is small, the cauldron cannot enter.
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if the expansion of a iron a little, and put in a tent of the Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilicon ointment, as it is expanded;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so that the ointment can enter easily:
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is pierced: let the cup or bowl be above, so that it is lower than the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is drawn to its full extent, if it does not slip.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the loins with your hands as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then appear in such a way that the bow runs to the lowest level it can reach,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is drawn to its full extent, if it does not slip.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast with a cloth as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bow doesn't fall off to one side: let the bow hang loosely forward, and don't tie anything to it.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medications to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and are placed over a linen drape that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then cut off as much of the breast as possible from the pit. That is, cut more away from the first than from the second.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then place a wound dressing above it. That is, another bandage according to the quantity of the breast pit,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the breast pit to adjust the bow. And do not remove the large bandage for more than a day or two;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one on top of the breast pit, remove often to remove the bandage;
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what runs from the bowels, whether it is poison or pus or enough or not enough or digested or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when this medicine has spread somewhat in the pit of the chest and you see the nature that comes out on the surface,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the breast is already sore, and bring the salve;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then let it down in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if change .i. other drape, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes upset after many days, knowing that the breast does not hurt.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poison enters after a long time, if it does not make you despair of your health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the sake of health. For there are men who delay healing by running into their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and they become indigent and weak after many days, knowing that their liver does not get better.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if their liver is delayed in healing and becomes inflamed, then take the following medicine: mix wet substances with moisture and dry them with virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as an antidote it finishes, for there is much vitriol, and that is the second medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a small piece of yellow brass, and form it with oil of roses, and rise it with equal old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then put it on and use it; and this same, once made into honey, cook it thicker,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when the finity of oil is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take mirr and aloe and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it over honey when it is taken off the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then in glue .i. drape, and put it over the chest, and once i administer on arista long,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the celestial plant, which is also like wheat flour and hundredweight;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in the use of simples or compounds: grind them, and make powder of them, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and this cure is long, and is not cured by this cure,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Then you will know that corruption is complete, and it affects the bone, or hard members, or limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if one practices the cure for a fistula, as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail bed of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	is an abscess that forms at the base of the finger nails on the palms of the hands
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Here is the translation of the text:
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when he has been wounded, and no attention is taken, then
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and cut and grind so that it cuts the root of the nail, and by chance cuts all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion up to the bone, until there is a stinking pain, and the two cheeks are wide apart, and the color flees.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the chapter on treatment, and the cure does not benefit.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If it is necessary that you cut off all the excess which has been retained by the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the finger pushes down on the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleeds.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	if you put the rag on top of the finger that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pour a little fire onto it, and hold it carefully and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top of the remaining flesh some fiery and corrosive medicine to destroy everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the healer apply garlic poultices until he is well.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corrosion is in the bone, then let him be cut and treated with fire, for as long as the bone is corroded, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the corruption of the flesh, then cut it off with a sharp blade, as it is said before:
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then let the healer apply garlic poultices until he is well.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and bruised, and it smells of great pain, then you must first heal it;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut off the nail from the spur with a saw across it;
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the saw does not come too close to the nailbed, because the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is something, put something on it to ease it;
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the palm of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two joints that may break in the hands of some men are both bone and flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by accident they may break or dislocate, but never have any fingers,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and in neither of the two do the roots of the joints arise, or their birth is in either of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Whoever is born with two testicles does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and whoever is born with the testicles joined together may move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of whoever is chubby so is light in some way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	size the in its root from a wide spathule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born with a joint root are difficult to treat; if you hold them down with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In those who are born or are wounded in the derriè, it is necessary that you first chop the flesh roundly up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, cut the bone with a suitable chisel and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The limbs that come together by nature, by the joining of a wound, by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you think you can take this sulfur, so that it is repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two blankets or sheets wet with oil, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin sheets of leather, until the leathers are stuck together, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The sulfur must be taken so that it is repaired according to its natural forms;
Des vils	Of the vile things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Are those that are full of excess melancholy, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more are found in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, while others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not administer any purging of the colon, and then the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure for fever is according to .ij. ways: one is that of the cupping, and force the black blood out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way if you open the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size should be according to this method: raise the first leg with hot water very strongly, until the big vein is visible,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	and then strain the leg of the sick person from above the hip all the way down to the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein at one inch, or two, or three, of a large size.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then slice and draw forth the black blood from your hand, from one wrist to the other, as much as the patient can endure;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it off, and instruct him to dye his meat with black coal;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and then begin the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are clean, and tie on the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	"Then dip it or bathe it, and let it dry: remove the leg from the hot water until it turns red, and inflame the veins;"
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	"If you do not have a bath, then heat it by the fire, and then rub the vein at the top of the thigh, or in the region of the ankle bone;"
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	"Then soak the skin with oil, and peel off the vein from each part, until it is completely exposed, so that one can feel it;"
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is red and black when it enters or leather so too as a white rope;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pour the oil out so that it is elevated from the leather, and then put on the knife lightly,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then take another piece of oil on top of it, two feet away; then scrape the leather along the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then let it hang by its thread, as you did before, and put on another knife, as you did first;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	and take another height, or more than you need then reduce it, and cut at both ends of the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	and then cut and trim down to the second height; then remove it from height to height until it is completely done, and then cut;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot raise and stretch it, then take a very strong and sharp needle,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and cut and trim it, and wrap it with thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is done;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and let it not break, because if it breaks, we cannot pull or lift it, and this is harmful to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished treating it, put wet wool in wine and oil over the wound and bandage it; and heal it until it is well.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if it is twisted and bent and wrapped together, and is not straightened, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must split it open, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron from which one makes a weapon if it is curved, and does not cut anything except that it cuts the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is a thick curve, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but since it is thick as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it may happen elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the poultice that comes off the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it enters the body coiling and going down, prevent between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of this illness are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then change the legs, and begins the illness to come out, also like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, if it is convenient that you wrap around a piece of cloth from one third to almost two thirds, and tie it off,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth hanging down at the leg, and as often as it comes off, if the wrap around the cloth and the tie
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you take a part of it, and wrap around the remainder, and do not cover all the way up to its root, until it is all wrapped up;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, if it enters into the pit, and brings about pus and rot, or bad disease there;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this reason it is necessary that she be treated little by little up to the neck, and nothing remains or cors.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and never once has this happened when she was treated with long palms, or with .x.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and some of them came to me, who was treated with long palms, and when you cut them, if they are a little raised or dented, and pierce them only up to the root,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	then let it be empty; and the matter that is within, and bring medicines to the place of corruption every day, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never cut at the vein with a knife; leastwise when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot is.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and that it may not break through and hurt him, then heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that come between the hide and the cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	is called in our land "buff disease", because it often occurs in buffaloes
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm which is born between the hide and the skin, and goes all over the body ascending and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he smells badly from member to member as far as he rips the hide where he went, and jumps far.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is infected with some humor, so that it comes towards and crawls and wriggles and worms or scabies.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its evil, for when it goes through the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance, it enters and destroys the oil; and such a thing often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him curable and extractable, so you can only do it when he goes.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So it is necessary that you lay him down on a firm bed tightly tied up,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then put a glass of wine in his mouth, and let him drink; and put the little dagger in his hand,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery, as long as it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm that it does, if it correts the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see coming to the head near the oil, then hold it fast with the hand; then lift it up and throw it away;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use the medicine to dissolve the pains of evil spirits with soluble medicines for evil spirits;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and to prevent meat from putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vaporization" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it spreads from member to member; and I saw the one I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a sick woman, and I discovered a small swelling on her arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then, I saw it rise up like a worm in the shoulder;
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	so quickly that it seemed alive, and as if it were silver when it cut from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left the body, and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it corrode all over the body until it reaches the other side;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that she twisted around again inside the body, as I saw it myself.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how much she moved from one member to another, for I had never seen such a disease move in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I know of many who have suffered from this illness, and they often experience pain that moves from one part to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I don't want to, if I saw it on a woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman's body was dry and the veins were exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason it appears that she has wind or gas in her bowels.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not appear to those who are delicious and have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you have healed this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the ligature above and remove them properly, and then cut off so much as it feels constrained to its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see blood,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of those who cause wind, like pills of putrid wine, and pills of horse chestnut, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the direction of their flight.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of arrows is such that there are some with large tips, and others with small, and some with hooks, and some riveted.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with .ij. points, and those with tongues, and those with pieces of wood attached;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one who bites in any member so bite according to .ij. manners: or in member principle hair bit,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she bites therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary that you wash yourself from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not perfectly extracted, if you pull it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	and the sign of the skull when the arrow enters and pierces the bone, and the medicine that is on the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when paralysis and weakness and twitching and redness in the eyes, and cramp and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is lost from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and springing out of the moist wound, white, resembling pulses, and jumping also like burned hay;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign will announce to you, if you continue with the treatment, and treat the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it bites or curls, is that it is near the left breast, and also because it seems to be stuck in something hard, not in something hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if by chance the arrow sounds like pulses, and in black blood, and cold comes and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	And so there is doubt of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow is that it does not hurt in the place of pain, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he sighs and shudders with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters in the shell of the chest, then the small ribs ache; and there is great pain and sighing; and all the members move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters in the stomach, perhaps there is food that does not digest.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters the belly, and does not go through the intestine's passage, there is no hope for healing or extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters the bladder, and the urine flows out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the aid and the spine and the force and the hips and the legs, and the limb resembling, are safe according to multiple provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it does not cause pain, listen to what I will tell you, for if you do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man who had an arrow lodged in his throat at the root of his neck.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and pulled the fat from the ear on another side, and was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I tried an arrow, which went into his oil of the ear, pulling out paper from his tongue.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was withdrawn, and I only felt the tip go towards his fist.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and was this arrow of a turquoise color, so that it would pass through the ears without causing any harm; and there were no bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And shot an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and was this Arabic arrow to the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I aimed at the beard, and made a subtle shot, and I hit the Christian:
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And shot an arrow to a man, which was either at the head or in the belly, and thought he was dead;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then let it pass .xxx. days, if not its disposition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrowhead, and sharpened it, and inserted it, and didn't have a bad accident.
