Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a bird with an arrow in its throat or back, and the wound is well healed;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and let the arrowhead stay inside it, and don't change its natural position;
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	There is no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom an arrow hit in the face, and was sore wounded;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And he remained there suffering great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And throw an arrow at the king of the princes, who was shot through the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was a little sagging on the right side; and the arrow was all re-sheathed
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the cure after she had been lame for three days. There was a very narrow wound.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I treated her with a subtle poultice, and I did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt pain and a headache on the right side.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought this was of the point of an arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on top of him a plastron made of resinous and digestive substances, so that his limbs do not inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the point of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the resinous plaster every day, and quickly healed the wound, and delayed the recovery of the patient for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he felt the arrow .i. during his life; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied to the wound a corrosive agile medicine by hands, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tested it, and felt the arrow's head which had become stuck;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied to the wound by that agile medicine, as long as the arrow's head was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and pass well the boundaries within .iiij. months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then he healed if the wound that I put the nails, and the meat on both sides and can't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I ceased from subtility and invention of means for instruments, until I took .i. day to make nails well;
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to him whose form will come at the end of this chapter of chalk, until I tra' it, and restore the wound;
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I see young people whose cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and it was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or have you said the quality of extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on what I do not say, for the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	But the wise masters compare only a little bit of salt, and on what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Truly nine ovre and nine instruments are necessary for the dismemberment of strange things which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the arrows should not be shot from the members unless they are prepared according to the nine ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that leap forth from there where they enter, it is arrows entering into their flesh, and do not leap at all now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap now, let it remain as the flesh decays within, and let the exit be closed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let it remain so for some days, and change the wound every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if there is any pain within, let the flesh be stretched out, and then cut off.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow has gone through the bone of the skull, and goes down to one of the chambers of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said happen to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it as long as it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes only to the sinews, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow has gone through only part of the bone, and does not go any further than the sinews,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and let the patient remain for some days without any bad accident if the machine of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she is so torn that she cannot come out, then administer tarred thread, as I told you; then treat the joint as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the chest if we cannot see it, and we seek it with all our might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, and treat it with appropriate tools;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by stretching the wound, and by the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	or there is no bone, nor nerve, nor vein, so that the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and if you can extract the arrow, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so that the bone is broken on either side where the arrow goes in, which you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or rain the ears of the arrow, as long as you can draw it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, that you pull it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, so that the ear of the arrow is completely cut off, then pull it, because extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of extraction makes you uncomfortable, so bring the following that we have said about the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put no comment that you may draw out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or red-hot or fiery-hot or firmly or loudly; and set the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow hit him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot, then follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, which opens nothing, or whose skin is swollen in a particular place, so that it can be seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	So cut it off above, until the scissors can take hold, and then remove it: if you wait any longer.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is held in the bone, turn your hand in a circle until it enters the bone and expands it, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot be removed, let it go for a while, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is the arrow that is stuck, pull it out with all your might;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if he is cut, and you see to administer poultices, if he administers them. I.e. an instrument sharpens,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow goes into the hair of the instrument; and then pour out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, pour out the instrument with a point entering in, to cheer the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches, so that you cut all the skin around where the venom is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	and then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow is caught in the breast or in the belly or in the bladder or on the side, and it is nearby, then you may cover it up with a cloth, if you can.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, for that is the task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the clamps used to treat arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and it should be like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do this: large, small, and medium-sized, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the claw that catches the arrow is also like the beak of an owl,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	for the tip of the arrow, as this is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the claw for holding and for keeping safe this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the veins of the neck common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one is healed are .xxxi., because it has head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is what the text says about the veins of the neck: "It is known as the 'herbech', which means two veins that run behind the ears."
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 18 arteries which are in the 2 temples.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 18 veins that are in the 2 arms of the two hands, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 18 veins which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the .ij. veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the .ij. veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly talked about are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cerebral, and it is on the left side of the neck, and it is called by the lay people "voinne du chef";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and its name is called 'fast', and it is composed of the cephalic and basal.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it 'vein of the neck'; and the basilical if it is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it 'vein of the abdomen', and it is on the light side.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that is opened, which is clearly visible above the breastbone.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little finger is the vein between the thumb and the index finger, and if it is at .ij. rain;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and where the foot are .iij. veins: one is dislocated from the socket of the left shin,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second that is in the ankle of the right leg; and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other leg;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are 3 veins dislocated from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The headache from the veins behind the ears is helped by the catarrh of the ancient and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the headache, as I told you, is that you remove the head of the illness.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with an asperous cloth; then tie the patient's neck with a rope,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the .iij. veins appear behind the ears depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Keep your hands on either side of your neck, and when you feel the pulse on one side, mark it with your finger.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the scalpel, and pierce through the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand up to the whole vein upstream.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and clean the meat and the vein thoroughly. Cut two times, and make sure there is no blood left.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then stretch and tie it, until it is healthy again.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have said above the incision and the fire cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The sine of the .ij. arteries that are in the .ij. temples, if it is an old migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sodom and eyes used to water, and to the eyes' tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the sight is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient draws out his neck, as long as the .ij. veins appear open.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and send blood to the two hands, and then sign of pain in the face;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift up the cup to your two hands, and then sign of pain on the top of the index finger, and pour the blood away from the cup,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the cup, and the cloth, as you have done in the .ij. other veins, and make the blood run according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then unclothe the patient, and set your two fingers on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then make the form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their grafting and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The relief from a vein in the forehead is as good as that from a headache of old age, and from migraine, and from jaundice;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient's neck twists when extracting it, so that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let out as much blood as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then cut the neck of the patient, and tie the vein so that it is clean and never again does a wide flame occur.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too hot; and the vein should be cut across, because the bone is close by, and the flame might break when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The first sentence to translate:
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is that the patient should break his neck with no rope, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	and then the doctor, and be careful when handling him, a little of the long flame, a little wide, for there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, in case of a break; then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then put it on cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The wound of the vein is so hot that it causes burning, and it also causes fever and facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as headaches and redness that come on in the face, and even when they are old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the wound is such that the patient hurts his neck, then he holds his baby with his left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long, flexible flame, and burn it between the two nostrils;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well and now the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not cut too deeply either, and make the blood flow according to your need, then let it rest for one night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The five kinds of wounds: the first, second, third, and fourth degrees of injury from cutting, burning, and scratching, and many diseases, and inflammation, and ulcers, and gangrene.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of health is such that the patient pulls his hair out from one side and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and so the master standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient cuts with .i. scythe
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the long vein slightly, then treat the wound quickly, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same on the other side, then hold the ligature, and tighten the ligature slightly,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	to strangle the sick person; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	of the healing of the skin
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	the healing of the veins in the mouth, and the corruption of the gums, and the splits in the lips, and the neck and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	and the qualities of the healing: to make the sick person sit before you, and to hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	and turn the lip, and look at 1 . 2 veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know them by this that they are black, and by this that there are small veins black around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So therefore know them both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So therefore take the larger of the two, and also do the same for the 1 2 veins that are above and below, because this is a similar way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Of the health of the tongue: that is to say, after the treatment for headaches, which are caused by the opening of the veins in the head, and it concerns the extraction from the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the healer is that the patient swallows between your hands before the sun, and he makes the tongue relax, and looks carefully at each side of a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So heal them both, and do not become too perfect, for soon the veins will be cut.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	Veins which are commonly treated are done according to .i. two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with fire a little flame sharp, or olive oil subtle as for cut-coves, and is called "aneasil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the largeness and stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fire sharp is so called, and is large as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is a good work to open the veins of the head which are flat and full of big blood and tumult.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle in point, and it is to save the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The salve of the temple, which is one of these veins, helps against diseases that are in the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is fitting for the surgeon to cut away the blood, and to bind up the wound, and not to be afraid of the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he stops the artery, and blood flows from it, if it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be struck with fire, but cut off as I said.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base does not open clearly, if it is necessary to stretch it out, and change one another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and wrap the fire in silk, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you are able to recognize the place of the injury, so that you can draw out the arm, and touch the place while recognizing the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the location of the injury, then lay the arm down, and wrap the wound in fire silk.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard against injuring in the artery when you see the edge broken, for it is from the artery: avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	and if you see coming up above as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	so hasten then, and put your hand on it with your palm up, and then open your hand so that the blood does not run; for it often happens:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	take hold of his arm, and let it be, and do not move the patient; and be in fear, and do not move him until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it does not stop, it will come to you, and the medicine is not given to you, because the chief of the retentives stops it; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fir tree bark, and make it, and take one of its halves and tie it well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding stops, it is good; if not, apply the powder that stops blood, as we have said;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the blood is not due to many disorders because of the small size of the wound and the pulse of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The patient should go to the doctor mid-way through the vein, and from the heart's base.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	For it is composed of the basal and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the doctor should wrap it tightly around the nerve that is exposed, and if he cuts too much, the nerve will burst;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the patient's legs become gray, and perhaps it cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, it is necessary that you heal the nerve from the instrument anaesthetized; and avoid the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the .i.. nerves, let it be cut short.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the head when helped, that it pulls blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal by touching the olive flame or the pine tree flame, because it is the one that saves all veins, because it does not burn the nerve or the artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	All the same, one must seek out the lighter case and not grieve over it if one makes a mistake the first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And so that the joints of the shoulders do not swell for some men if one makes a mistake the first time, but it is not necessary to grieve.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health so much depends on your belief.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about a doctor, if is that medicine is only to be used to maintain health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to ward off future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the doctor should make one of the three incisions that are on the head: that is to say, cephalic, temporal, and basal;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the doctor should make one of these three incisions when the patient has just eaten, in autumn and winter after eating, as soon as the sign of satiety appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and the doctor should make one of these three incisions the first day or third day after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The health of a person who has recovered from disease is not determined by the time of day or season; but rather, it is in all hours and times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it does not suit to cure children until they are .xxiii years old, nor women but four months after childbearing until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It does not suit to cure the old who have passed .lx. years, for they should be left alone.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when any person is cured, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that he take a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is still some food in his mouth, so that the veins do not draw the excessive fluids that are harmful to the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not heal those who are too sore from meat, nor those who are drunk, as much as they need to be healed, nor those who drop their fluids.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is not healing after a feverish passion, and vomiting, and abdominal discomfort, and multiple trips to the bathroom, and sleeping and fasting, and whatever else impedes him.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly adjust the humors, if he is overweight, through meat, drinking, and medicine, if you have it.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	and then enter the bath, if nothing is harmful to him, because it weakens the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal from the wound at the back of the neck by the third day, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect him on days of work, and from hunger, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be lying and jointed, and let the healer be higher than he who is healed, and wash his arms.11 times or 13 times,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then remove the ligature with care, for when it is too tight or too loose, he cannot run without it.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with his hands, until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	and then dip the wound in a small cup of old oil, and then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein to stop the bleeding,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not run and does not bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run out like strings from the body, and if they are of such a nature that they are prone to windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one applies fire to them, if one takes it away, the vein cannot be opened, and so they are of this kind;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if one opens the vein, if it is too narrow, for one thing, so that the blood flows out, and also
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, if one begins again a little more slightly or on an ambulance, if the veins are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if it swells up, and the patient hopes, let him lie one or two days, and bind not his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	For in case there come abscesses; do not enter a bath, but begin again the treatment if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the fracture is small, or the joint is slightly dislocated, and you doubt whether it will move as much as you see, so that the fire may be applied to all the fracture without pain;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and make a small wound, so that the swelling is less when the wound is made; for this often occurs, when the wound is small:
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound open, then do not recommend the use of salt, and put a little oil on it, because it dries up the blood in this place where the oil is placed.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and so administer the oil to each wound that you heal the veins to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and so it makes a triple and bowing sound when you put it on the wound; if it is too thick, it makes a subtle sound and splits when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there is a large abscess, which often comes when the opening of the vein is small, then it must be done;
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put on the shoulder a wet sponge in water and in hemp a little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood flowing from a vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any black or green, so no harm to it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on anything of aloe or myrrh made up of juice of calamus, monkshood, or something like it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often the appendix and the appearance towards the side of the base: put your hand there, and if you feel the soft spot under pressure from your hand, that is the appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So then you must not put anything on any of what we have said, for by chance in the heart without the artery; but make it .i. plaster dry so that it hardens the place, and then heal it with other cures until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it stay until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are healthy and have the need to extract blood, let them make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to heal them little by little, and one should heal them by cutting across, not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of healing is preserved from the decay of blood and the hurting of nerves, and it is better than the long surgery does not do wide cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to him whose course needs surgery, it is necessary to give moist wine in grape juice; if he is heated, if he has a fever, drink three times or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexions, if he drinks moist wine before the surgery in musk syrup, or honey syrup with aromatic spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he sweats to sickness, after the flow of blood, it is convenient that he hums brew of car, and syrupy scent.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use of other things which we have said in the chapter or paste for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up a arm, and sweats sometimes, if it is convenient, when he is weakened by great sickness, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue which continues continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he vomits up an arm after the first sickness, and he has a strong body, if he heals in 6 hours after the first sickness, or in 7 hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who must be healed from another side, if he must be healed on the second day or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has blood flowing inside his body which is heated up and causes fever. If this happens, a large amount must be extracted, and the opening made so wide that it can pass through with ease.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and then you must perform all the conditions for healing, and put your hand on his pulse as he heals, so that death does not come from pain.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when healing is neglected.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the dislocation of the arm, and make it come out again without the second time, and the hole is closed, that you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is curved, that he extends the arm carefully, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it rest until the second time it is well; or you put to it at the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that has been frozen by the opening flows again;
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .I. piece of silk, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, leave it and do not tighten it, as long as the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if need be to drain the blood a second time, if the vein is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is called the "chief vein," and it should not be punctured for drainage.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of the drain is that the patient dips his hand in warm water, so that the feverish color disappears.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	And so let it move gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then he keeps it now from top to bottom, not wide or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be careful not to hurt the joint of the hand, and don't let it get wet, put the hand in warm water, and leave the blood running in the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's cold, don't put the hand in warm water, because we put it more in summer than in winter;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and this vein is safer from all other veins, that there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salve of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is its method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Exhaust the hand, and dip it in warm water until the vein has disappeared, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And bend it across, and cut it all over, if it doesn't harm anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And don't cut too deep, for the nerve are all exposed from the core;
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put hand in warm water, he is still frozen in the wound, and can not pull it out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if put on the vein oil and thread to sew it tightly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgeon must remove the disease from the patient's left hand, and do everything as I have told you before the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	And the surgeon must remove all diseases that are below the belt,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	If it is a disease of the hips, and retention of flowers, and a disease of the kidneys, and of the feet and legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his health is that the patient should drink some hot water, and rub the vein until it stops.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the joint at the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cure it on the stone, be careful of the knots that are loose, and cure it by traversing as when digging; and let the fire burn away.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot be drained, put the stone in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is cured the first time, start the second time above a little hole, because the leech is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the strength, as we have said, and make the same treatment with the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The legs of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle joint, and its pain reaches the knee, when it is due to injury.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this pain is such that the patient enters or leaves by the foot, and it is pulled out from under the ankle. If there is twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the nerve does not open; and if it opens, so that you can feel it with your fingers in all directions, and going across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it makes a sound when you touch it, for the leg is exposed, and it is very soft to the touch.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't treat it, so that there is no rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard against the nails;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much damage to the leg that you can see it, then cut the ligature, and place cotton and hold it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Sores from suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or glass, or quartz; and the suction is made in one of two ways: either by wounding and drawing out blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which is not to hurt if it is according to .ij. manners: or she is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation that is made by hurting and by extraction of blood if it is made in .xiiij. degrees of the heart,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	from which one is all in sum the chief; and others is in mid the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and .ij. others in .ij. costois du cou; et le ventouse desoez le menton;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cups of the shoulders; and the suction cup over the collarbones;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction cups around the biceps; and the suction cups around the thighs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups around the ankles; and the suction cup does not treat blood flow, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the body;
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason do not block it completely, as is done with vein surgery;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that she be amenable, nor that there be any fire or heat, in any disease that comes from overfullness, until the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if for a necessity of diseases it is necessary to ventilate, or by customs, let us amenable each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and emit and in every season;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have the need to ventilate, become much heavier;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who, when they truevent, come from repletion and pain in their face, and in their head, and darkness of eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who drink a drop of blood in their mouth, and have fled the tongue, and thirst for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people, and see no blood and vomit and die and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is half past midnight, we command them to fast for 2 hours that day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saint of the muse helps with grief in the heart ... but it is not until all blood has been evacuated from the body that he comes to the aid of those who are grieved.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in the place of the health of the cerebral,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not suffice that he who is of a cold complex use this, or who has a fever, because this does him much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this purpose neither the old nor those who have cold diseases should use it,
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is often treated with this, if he becomes dizzy, and for this reason one should place the cautery a little more down by the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventilation of the neck is in place at the base of the skull and the basilica, and for this reason it goes to the extraction of the foot.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and with a cut of the channel of the palm, and all, and repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to press down, because if it holds too tightly, then in the stomach or the heart or the chest.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventilation of the neck is in place at the base of the skull and the basilica, and for this reason it goes to the extraction of the foot.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the place of the sanctity of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command to the saint that he express his hand at the putting on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not take away blood with a wound.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the mouth bring to disease of the mouth and corruption of the gums and similar diseases which are in the mouth; and is at the place of the sanctities of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the shoulders bring to disease that comes from heat and filling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the collar bring as much as the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For she draws out blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for his veins are naked and can be easily cut through, and know how to tie off arteries and veins.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup placed on the back is suitable for sucking out the foundation blood, and the pus from the abscesses, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large and made of leather, so that it has the ability to well suck; and by chance, if it were too thin, it would break, and would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs open widely, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are suitable for the old pains of the knees, and of the ankles, and of the bladder, and turn back the flowers; and they are in place of the 12th bone, and of the 12th joint, and moreover they weaken the body greatly after a long time, and bring about premature death in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Here is the translation of the provided Old French text into English:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is thick, then you must hurt it once with a sharp instrument; the first time to cut through the thick vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick, then you must hurt it a third time; and when we want to squeeze the blood out little by little, then we must press hard once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And when we want to squeeze the blood out little by little, then we must press often; and if it is thick, then we must firmly press until the veins burst suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and to those who have thick leather and tough skin, that you anoint the joints of the suction cups with oil which opens and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in a state of stiffness, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in a state of tension, of nettle oil, or of lily oil, or of chamomile, or other similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then take oil of almonds, or of myrrh, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if someone has a tender back and large pores, it is not appropriate to put any oil on it,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is appropriate to wash after the wind has passed with rose water, or cold water, or water from a mulberry tree, or water from a cucumber, or porcelain water, or other similar water.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if one has moisture due to sweat, if it rises thus, or with water from mistletoe, and sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if one has excessive fluids, they rise from old wine, or water from fennel, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not appropriate to use a suction cup before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or .ij.; and do not sleep after the suction.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is appropriate that he warm up, when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And warn if the one who is being treated is coleric, and if his skin is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is appropriate that he drink cold things, like grapes, endive, lettuce, and sage, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mint juice, and cheese curds, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cool complexion, if they drink honey syrup, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and mint juice, and mint curds and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and let him drink as much as he can when the wind blows, for he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is appropriate to give some people triple or musk-flavored food before or after exposure to the wind, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful with the sun, but it only works if you're hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are used to hurt are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and podagra, and the belly, and the bowels, and the anus, for this member does not suffer to be hurt on the skin.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it only to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do when we put leeches on the breast when there is no pain; by removing the viscosity that is in the member, as we put leeches on the belly and the bowels to weaken the member,
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone the pain, when there is an operation or stone, if bone by its own power attracts the operation, or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so it is done when you put it on the liver and on the stomach when there is wind repressed,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are emptied only to suck up; and never are they emptied together fire, and never is plain water drawn,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as if for the diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way that the suction cup is filled with hot water, or with water in which herbs have been boiled suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup is made from this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has .ij. two inches in diameter and a palm's width across the top, and it has an orifice at the center about as wide as a pin, just as to pass through a needle
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of brass, smooth before so that it does not bruise the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and has in the center a crossbar of brass or iron, to hold a candlestick
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and may they be great and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the sucks of children are other than those of old men, and leaner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this suck must be put on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candlewax or liniment, and place it between the thumb and finger at the top of the thumb, which is placed between the thumb and finger,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	So that the clarity is at the bottom of the vacuum so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and your two are on the hole that we have said, so that when you press, if there is steam, and then take off the vacuum;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining as before, and recommence it often, if you need to do so.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the vacuum that has been prepared for pleurisy, there is no verge or pit, and it is only prepared when it is plain of water, and is placed on the member as little as possible;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	are not adjusted except in limbs where it is impossible to put a suction cup due to their smallness, as in the case of lips and gums, and similar things;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the case of naked limbs of horses, as in the case of two or three-year-old horses, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is that when you find suction cups that are in smooth, clear waters without danger, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put a nut in the water until they are familiar with it, and do not have anything in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then rub the member until it is red, and put on the poultices.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are healed and have become strong, one can then use a blister, for it is useful after that.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the member thus, and then dip it in water well, and then squeeze it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it is left too long after the heart of the body, so wet .i. linen cloth in cold water and put on, until the heart has dried up;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if it increases, so put on vitriolic paste or gangrene and similar things until it has dried up;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the middle of peas peeled, and let them burn at the fire for now they will dry up;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work, then take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the sutures do not want to take hold, then rub the site of the cut with fresh blood or stick an needle in it as long as there is no blood.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and soon as they feel the pain, so they start to burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, then powder a little aloe and wormwood, or ash, so they will stop crying now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapter on cauterization is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is used for restoring breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, o son of a scholar, that the wise men poured this chapter on cauterization upon you, that you have never read such in any of the old books, nor have you ever read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange to us in our land, for I never found any good book about it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except by the science of the ancient books, from which I have studied and practiced the art, and through experience, and through the customs of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have condensed it at the end, and have clearly depicted the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these twenty-nine chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the sum of words and chapters where the sage places his understanding, and delays on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when there is a break, dislocation, twisting, or distortion in someone, it is necessary for you to hurry to save the patient from pain on both sides, if anything does not prevent him from walking, as weakness of the spine, or infirmity, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if his legs are too tight or too loose; and he should not eat cold dishes, nor drink wine, nor eat any greasy foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the appendix, nor about the expansion of matter in the member; if the patient returns to his usual governance that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken nose begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meat that heals well, or has viscosity like cooked bread, and rice, and peas, and pies made from cheese, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nutrition, the break will heal faster and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken nose of old or weak people cannot heal or harden the members well according to their nature, nor those that are too tender, as is the case with the nose of small children;
